(3) The restriction of $X _ { J } / S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ to $S _ { J + \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ is identified with an analytic neighbourhood of the vertex in the restriction of the family $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ given by Theorem 2.28, (1) with ${ \mathfrak { D } } = { \mathfrak { D } } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ , for each $N \geq 0$ .

Proof.
(1) We use the notation of Example 1.10, so that the pair $( Y , D )$ determines an infinite fan $\tilde { \Sigma }$ in $M _ { \mathbb { R } }$ with the primitive generators of the rays being the $v _ { i }$ for $i \in \mathbb Z$ .
We also have $T \in { \mathrm { S L } } ( M )$ acting on the fan $\tilde { \Sigma }$ .
We have $B = | \tilde { \Sigma } | / \Gamma$ , where $\Gamma$ is the group generated by $T$ .

Now as in $\ S 7 . 1$ , let $\Xi \subset M _ { \mathbb { R } }$ be the convex hull of the points $v _ { i } \in M$ .
Thus $\Xi$ is an infinite convex polytope.
Let $\widetilde { \Sigma } ^ { \prime }$ be the subdivision of $\Xi$ induced by $\tilde { \Sigma }$ .
In what follows, we will build a Mumford degeneration $Z / S _ { J }$ with special fibre $Z _ { 0 }$ the stable toric variety associated to $\widetilde { \Sigma } ^ { \prime }$ .
In other words, $Z _ { 0 }$ will be the union of the toric surfaces associated to the maximal polytopes in $\widetilde { \Sigma } ^ { \prime }$ .

$S _ { J }$ is the affine toric variety associated to the face $\sigma _ { \mathrm { b d y } } : = \sigma _ { P } \cap L ^ { \perp }$ of $\sigma _ { P }$ , and $P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } : = \sigma _ { \mathrm { b d y } } \cap A _ { 1 } ( Y , \mathbb { Z } )$ contains the classes of the components of the boundary of $Y$ .
We define a piecewise linear convex function $\tilde { \varphi } \colon | \tilde { \Sigma } ^ { \prime } |  P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \otimes _ { \mathbb { Z } } \mathbb { R }$ by restriction of a piecewise linear convex function $\tilde { \varphi }$ on $| \tilde { \Sigma } |$ .
This function is the single-valued representative for $\varphi$ on the universal cover of $B _ { 0 }$ , and as such, is defined up to an integral linear function by specifying its bending parameter

$$
\kappa _ { \tilde { \varphi } , \rho _ { i } } = [ D _ { i \mathrm { m o d } n } ] \in P _ { \mathrm { b d y } }
$$

if $\rho _ { i } = \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } v _ { i }$

Then $\tilde { \varphi }$ determines a Mumford degeneration: this is a slight generalization of §1.3.
One defines

$$
\begin{array} { r } { \tilde { \Xi } : = \{ ( m , r ) | m \in \Xi , r \in \tilde { \varphi } ( m ) + \sigma _ { \mathrm { b d y } } \} \subset M _ { \mathbb R } \oplus ( P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \otimes _ { \mathbb Z } \mathbb R ) . } \end{array}
$$

Let $C ( \tilde { \Xi } )$ be the closure of

$$
\begin{array} { r } { \{ ( s m , s r , s ) | ( m , r ) \in \tilde { \Xi } , s \geq 0 \} \subset M _ { \mathbb { R } } \oplus ( P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \otimes _ { \mathbb { Z } } \mathbb { R } ) \oplus \mathbb { R } . } \end{array}
$$

Then $\mathbb { C } [ C ( \tilde { \Xi } ) \cap ( M \oplus P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \oplus \mathbb { Z } ) ]$ has a natural grading given by the last coordinate, and the degree zero part of this ring is easily seen to contain $\mathbb { C } [ P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ]$ .
Thus we obtain the Mumford family determined by $\bar { \varphi }$ a s

$$
Z : = \mathrm { P r o j } \mathbb { C } [ C ( \tilde { \Xi } ) \cap ( M \oplus P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \oplus \mathbb { Z } ) ] \to \mathrm { S p e c } \mathbb { C } [ P _ { \mathrm { b d y } } ] = S _ { J } .
$$

One sees easily that the fibre over $0 \in S _ { J }$ of $Z  S _ { J }$ has infinitely many components indexed by the 2-cells of the subdivision $\widetilde { \Sigma } ^ { \prime }$ of $\Xi$ , each of which is a copy of the blowup of $\mathbb { A } ^ { 2 }$ at the origin.
The general fibre is a toric surface (only locally of finite type)

containing an infinite chain of smooth rational curves, which specializes to the union of the exceptional curves of the blowups in $Z _ { 0 }$ .
By construction $\Gamma$ acts on $Z$ over $S _ { J }$ (because $\tilde { \varphi }$ is $\Gamma$ -invariant modulo integral affine functions).
Let $E \subset Z / S _ { J }$ be the family of curves described above (the relative toric boundary).
The group $\Gamma$ acts properly discontinuously on a tubular neighbourhood $N$ of $E \subset Z$ (cf.
[AMRT75], p.
48).
Let $p \colon ( F \subset { \tilde { X } } ) \to S _ { J }$ denote the quotient of $( E \subset N ) \to S _ { J }$ by $\Gamma$ .

The divisor $F \subset X$ is Cartier and the dual of its normal bundle is relatively ample over a neighbourhood of $0 \in S _ { J }$ .
Indeed, the special fibre $\tilde { X } _ { 0 }$ is a union of $n$ irreducible components each isomorphic to a tubular neighbourhood of the exceptional locus in the blowup of $\mathbb { A } ^ { 2 }$ , and $F _ { 0 } \subset \breve { X } _ { 0 }$ is the cycle of $n$ smooth rational curves formed by the exceptional curves of the blowups.
Hence the normal bundle of $F _ { 0 } ^ { \prime }$ in $\tilde { X _ { 0 } }$ has degree $- 1$ on each component of $F _ { 0 } ^ { \prime }$ .
Moreover, we have $R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } ( \mathcal { N } _ { F / \tilde { X } } ^ { \vee } ) ^ { \otimes k } = 0$ for each $k > 0$ .
Indeed, by cohomology and base change it suffices to show that $H ^ { 1 } ( ( \mathcal { N } _ { F _ { 0 } / \tilde { X } _ { 0 } } ^ { \vee } ) ^ { \otimes k } ) = 0$ , and this follows from Serre duality.
Now by a relative version of Grauert’s contractibility criterion [F75], Thm.
2, taking global sections of the structure sheaf defines a contraction $p \colon \tilde { X }  X _ { J } / S _ { J }$ to a family of Stein analytic spaces with exceptional locus $F ^ { \prime }$ .
The general fibre $X _ { J , t }$ of $X _ { J } / S _ { J }$ is the dual cusp by Lemma 7.3. The section $s : S _ { J } \to X _ { J }$ takes $x \in S _ { J }$ to the cusp of $X _ { J , x }$ .

We now show that $X _ { J } / S _ { J }$ is flat and the special fibre is the neighbourhood of the $n$ -vertex obtained by contracting $F _ { 0 } \subset \breve { X } _ { 0 }$ .
The key point is that $R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } }$ is a locally free $\mathcal { O } _ { S _ { J } }$ -module, cf.
[W76], Theorem 1.4(b). Indeed, we have

$$
R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } { \mathcal { O } } _ { \tilde { X } } ( - F ) = 0
$$

by cohomology and base change, the theorem on formal functions, and the vanishing $H ^ { 1 } ( ( \mathcal { N } _ { F _ { 0 } / \tilde { X } _ { 0 } } ^ { \vee } ) ^ { \otimes k } ) = 0$ for $k > 0$ used above.
So, pushing forward the exact sequence

$$
0 \to \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } } ( - F ) \to \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } } \to \mathcal { O } _ { F } \to 0
$$

we obtain

$$
R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } } = R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { F } \simeq \mathcal { O } _ { S _ { J } } .
$$

Recall that $S _ { J }$ is a toric variety, so in particular Cohen-Macaulay.
Let $t _ { 1 } , \ldots , t _ { r }$ be a regular sequence at $0 \in S _ { J }$ of length $\mathrm { d i m } S _ { J }$ and write

$$
S _ { J } ^ { i } = V ( t _ { 1 } , \cdot \cdot \cdot , t _ { i } ) \subset S _ { J } ,
$$

$\tilde { X } ^ { i } = \tilde { X } | _ { S _ { J } ^ { i } }$ , and let $X _ { J } ^ { i } / S _ { J } ^ { i }$ be the family over $S _ { J } ^ { i }$ defined by $O _ { X _ { J } ^ { i } } = p _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } ^ { i } }$ .
Arguing as above we find that $R ^ { 1 } p _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } ^ { i } } \simeq \mathcal { O } _ { S _ { J } ^ { i } }$ .
Pushing forward the exact sequence

$$
0  \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } ^ { i } } { \stackrel { \cdot \cdot t _ { i + 1 } } { \longrightarrow } } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } ^ { i } } { \longrightarrow } \mathcal { O } _ { \tilde { X } ^ { i + 1 } } { \longrightarrow } 0
$$

we deduce that the natural map

$$
\mathcal { O } _ { X _ { J } ^ { i } } / t _ { i + 1 } \mathcal { O } _ { X _ { J } ^ { i } } \to \mathcal { O } _ { X _ { J } ^ { i + 1 } }
$$

is an isomorphism.
Hence by the local criterion of flatness [Ma89], Ex. 22.3, p.
178, it suffices to show that $X _ { J } ^ { r } / S _ { J } ^ { r }$ is flat with special fibre the $n$ -vertex. But $S _ { J } ^ { r }$ is the spectrum of an Artinian $\mathbb { C }$ -algebra, so this follows from [W76], Theorem 1.4(b).

(2) Write $Z ^ { o } = Z \backslash E$ , and $m _ { i } = - D _ { i \mathrm { m o d } n } ^ { 2 }$ , $a _ { i } = z ^ { \left\lfloor D _ { i \bmod n } \right\rfloor }$ for $i \in \mathbb Z$ .
We have an open covering

$$
Z ^ { o } = \bigcup _ { i \in \mathbb { Z } } U _ { i , J } ,
$$

where

$$
U _ { i , J } = V ( x _ { i - 1 } x _ { i + 1 } - a _ { i } x _ { i } ^ { m _ { i } } ) \subset \mathbb { A } _ { x _ { i - 1 } , x _ { i + 1 } } ^ { 2 } \times ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { x _ { i } } \times S _ { J } .
$$

Similarly, we have an open covering

$$
Z = \bigcup _ { i \in \mathbb { Z } } { \bar { U } } _ { i , J } ,
$$

where

$$
\begin{array} { r l } & { \bar { U } _ { i , J } = V ( x _ { i - 1 } ^ { \prime } x _ { i + 1 } ^ { \prime } - a _ { i } x _ { i } ^ { m _ { i } - 2 } ) \subset \mathbb { A } _ { x _ { i - 1 } ^ { \prime } , x _ { i } , x _ { i + 1 } ^ { \prime } } ^ { 3 } \times S _ { J } , } \\ & { E \cap \bar { U } _ { i , J } = V ( x _ { i } ) \subset \bar { U } _ { i , J } , } \end{array}
$$

and $U _ { i , J } \ : \backslash \ : E = U _ { i , J }$ via $x _ { i - 1 } = x _ { i } x _ { i - 1 } ^ { \prime }$ , $x _ { i + 1 } = x _ { i } x _ { i + 1 } ^ { \prime }$ .
(Note that $m _ { i } = - D _ { i } ^ { 2 } \ge 2$ by assumption.)

Recall that the infinite cyclic group $\Gamma$ acts on $Z / S _ { J }$ , there is a $\Gamma$ -invariant tubular neighbourhood $N \subset Z$ of $E \subset Z$ on which the action is properly discontinuous, and $F \subset { \tilde { X } }$ is obtained as the quotient of $E \subset N$ by $\Gamma$ .
In terms of the open covering above the action is given by $U _ { i , J } \to U _ { i + n , J }$ , $x _ { j } \mapsto x _ { j + n }$ .
Note that the map $U _ { i , J } \cap N \to \tilde { X }$ is not an open embedding (because, for example, $U _ { i , J }$ contains the general fibre of $Z ^ { o } / S _ { J }$ ).
Fix $R > 1$ .
We define $W _ { i } \subset U _ { i , J } \cap N$ by

$$
W _ { i } = \{ ( x _ { i - 1 } , x _ { i } , x _ { i + 1 } ) \in U _ { i , J } \cap N \mid | x _ { i - 1 } | < R | x _ { i } | , | x _ { i + 1 } | < R | x _ { i } | \}
$$

and similarly define $\overline { { W } } _ { i } \subset \bar { U } _ { i , J } \cap N$ by

$$
\overline { { W } } _ { i } = \{ ( x _ { i - 1 } ^ { \prime } , x _ { i } , x _ { i + 1 } ^ { \prime } ) \in \bar { U } _ { i , J } \cap N \mid | x _ { i - 1 } ^ { \prime } | < R , | x _ { i + 1 } ^ { \prime } | < R \} .
$$

Then ${ \overline { { W } } } _ { i } \setminus E = W _ { i }$

The $\overline { { W } } _ { i }$ cover the special fibre $E _ { 0 }$ of $E / S _ { J }$ (using $R > 1$ ).
The open set $\bigcup \overline { { W } } _ { i } \subset N$ is $\Gamma$ -invariant, the quotient $( N , E ) \to ( \tilde { X } , F )$ by $\Gamma$ is a covering map, and $p \colon \dot { X }  X _ { J }$ is proper with exceptional locus $F ^ { \prime }$ .
Hence we may assume (passing to an analytic neighbourhood $S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ of $0 \in S _ { J }$ and $s ( 0 ) \in X _ { J }$ ) that $N = \cup \overline { { W } } _ { i }$ .

By Lemma 7.6 below there exists $\delta > 0$ such that

$$
W _ { i } \cap \{ ( x _ { i - 1 } , x _ { i } , x _ { i + 1 } ) | | x _ { i } | < \delta \} \subset \{ | x _ { j } | < 1 \quad \forall j \}
$$

for each $i$ .
We replace $\overline { { W } } _ { i }$ by $\overline { { W } } _ { i } \cap \{ | x _ { i } | < \delta \}$ , and modify $W _ { i }$ similarly.
Then as above we may assume that $N = \cup \overline { { W } } _ { i }$ , and $N \subset \{ | x _ { i } | < 1 \forall i \}$ .
We claim that $W _ { i } \cap W _ { j } = \emptyset$ for all $j > i + 1$ .
It suffices to work on the general fibre of $Z ^ { o } / S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ , which is an algebraic torus.
The coordinate functions $x _ { i }$ are characters of this torus (up to a multiplicative constant).
By construction we have $| x _ { i } | < 1$ for each $i$ on $N$ .
Hence, shrinking the base $S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ , we may assume that $| a _ { i } x _ { i } ^ { m _ { i } - 2 } | < 1 / R ^ { 2 }$ for each $i$ .
The relation

$$
x _ { i - 1 } x _ { i + 1 } = a _ { i } x _ { i } ^ { m _ { i } }
$$

gives the inequality

$$
| x _ { i + 1 } / x _ { i } | < ( 1 / R ^ { 2 } ) | x _ { i } / x _ { i - 1 } | .
$$

Combining such inequalities we obtain

$$
| x _ { j + 1 } / x _ { j } | < ( 1 / R ^ { 2 } ) ^ { j - i } | x _ { i + 1 } / x _ { i } | \mathrm { f o r } \ j > i .
$$

Now $| x _ { i + 1 } / x _ { i } | < R$ on $W _ { i }$ and $| x _ { j - 1 } / x _ { j } | < R$ on $W _ { j }$ , so $| x _ { j } / x _ { j - 1 } | > ( 1 / R ^ { 2 } ) | x _ { i + 1 } / x _ { i } |$ o n $W _ { i } \cap W _ { j }$ .
For $j > i + 1$ this contradicts the inequality (7.2), hence $W _ { i } \cap W _ { j } = \emptyset$ as claimed.

It follows that $W _ { i }$ embeds in $X _ { J }$ , using the fact that we have assumed $n \geq 3$ .
Let $V _ { i }$ denote its image, with indices now understood modulo $n$ .
Thus $X _ { J } ^ { o } = \cup V _ { i }$ and the inverse image of $V _ { i }$ is the (disjoint) union of $W _ { j }$ such that $j \equiv i$ mod $n$ .
We have $V _ { i } \cap V _ { j } = \emptyset$ for $j \neq i - 1 , i , i + 1$ by our claim above.
So, writing $V _ { \rho , J } : = V _ { i }$ for $\rho$ the ray of $\Sigma$ corresponding to $D _ { i }$ , the condition (2)(b) is satisfied.

(3) We have the open covering $X _ { J } ^ { o } = \cup V _ { i }$ and open embeddings $V _ { i } \subset U _ { i , J }$ , and an open covering $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } ^ { o } = \bigcup U _ { i , \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ .
The restrictions of $U _ { i , J } / S _ { J }$ and $U _ { i , \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ to $\operatorname { S } _ { J + \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ are identified, and the gluing maps coincide.
It follows that the restriction of $X _ { J } / S _ { J }$ is identified with a neighbourhood of the vertex in the restriction of $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ using Lemma 2.10. 

Lemma 7.6. We use the notation of the proof of Theorem $\boldsymbol { \mathscr { I } } . 5 ( \mathcal { 2 } )$ .
Let $x _ { j }$ be the coordinate functions on $Z ^ { o } = \cup U _ { i , J }$ .
There exists $\delta > 0$ such that on each open set $U _ { i , J }$ if $| x _ { i } | < \delta$ , $| x _ { i - 1 } | < R | x _ { i } |$ , $| x _ { i + 1 } | < R | x _ { i } |$ , and $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ for all $p \in P _ { \mathrm { b d y } }$ then $| x _ { j } | < 1$ for all $j$ .

Proof.
The points $v _ { i - 1 }$ , $v _ { i }$ , and $v _ { i + 1 }$ are consecutive integral points on the boundary of the infinite convex polytope $\Xi$ with asymptotic directions $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ .
It follows that $w _ { 1 } = \alpha _ { i 1 } v _ { i } + \beta _ { i 1 } ( v _ { i - 1 } - v _ { i } )$ and $w _ { 2 } = \alpha _ { i 2 } v _ { i } + \beta _ { i 2 } ( v _ { i + 1 } - v _ { i } )$ for some $\alpha _ { i 1 } , \beta _ { i 1 } , \alpha _ { i 2 } , \beta _ { i 2 } \in \mathbb { R } _ { > 0 }$ .
Note that the ratios $\beta _ { i 1 } / \alpha _ { i 1 } , \beta _ { i 2 } / \alpha _ { i 2 }$ only depend on $i$ modulo $n$ (because $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ are eigenvectors of $T$ and $T ( v _ { i } ) = v _ { i + n }$ ).
Let $\mu$ be the maximum of the ratios $\beta _ { i 1 } / \alpha _ { i 1 } , \beta _ { i 2 } / \alpha _ { i 2 }$ for $i = 1 , \ldots , n$ .
Let $\delta = R ^ { - \mu }$ .
If $j > i$ then $v _ { j } = \alpha v _ { i } + \beta ( v _ { i + 1 } - v _ { i } )$ with $\beta / \alpha < \beta _ { i 2 } / \alpha _ { i 2 }$ .
The coordinate function $x _ { j }$ can be written as $z ^ { p } x _ { i } ^ { \alpha } ( x _ { i + 1 } / x _ { i } ) ^ { \beta }$ on $V _ { i }$ , where $p \in P _ { \mathrm { b d y } }$ .
Thus $| x _ { j } | < \delta ^ { \alpha } R ^ { \beta } < 1$ for $| x _ { i } | < \delta$ and $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ .
The same is true for $j ~ < ~ i$ by symmetry.
$\boxed { \begin{array} { r l } \end{array} }$

7.3. Thickening of the cusp family.
We continue to work with the setup at the beginning of §7.2, with $( Y , D )$ , $L$ , $\sigma _ { P }$ , $P$ , $\mathfrak { m }$ and $J$ as given there.

Theorem 7.7. Let $p _ { J } \colon X _ { J } \to S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ be the analytic family of Theorem 7.5. Possibly after replacing $S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ by a smaller neighbourhood of $0 \in S _ { J }$ and $X _ { J }$ by a smaller neighbourhood of $s ( S _ { J } ^ { \prime } ) \subset X _ { J }$ , independent of the choice of $I$ below, the following holds.
Let $I \subset P$ be a monomial ideal such that $\sqrt { I } = J$ and let $S _ { I } ^ { \prime } \subset S _ { I }$ denote the induced thickening of $S _ { J } ^ { \prime } \subset S _ { J }$ .
There is an infinitesimal deformation $f _ { I } \colon X _ { I } \to S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ of $f _ { J } \colon X _ { J } \  \ S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ such that for each $N > 0$ the restriction to Spec $\mathbb { k } [ P ] / ( I + \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } )$ is identified with an analytic neighbourhood of the vertex in the restriction of the family $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ given by Theorem 2.28, (1) applied with ${ \mathfrak { D } } = { \mathfrak { D } } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ .

Proof.
As usual, $\mathfrak { D } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ is the canonical scattering diagram on $B$ associated to the pair $( Y , D )$ .
Note that the hypotheses (I) and (II) of Theorem 3.8 are satisfied for the ideal $J$ (but not (III)).
This is because we can take $\begin{array} { r } { L = A + \sum a _ { i } D _ { i } } \end{array}$ with $A$ ample on $Y$ and $a _ { i } > 0$ , and any $\mathbb { A } ^ { 1 }$ -class $\beta$ intersects the $D _ { i }$ non-negatively.
Then for any $k$ there are only a finite number of $\mathbb { A } ^ { 1 }$ -classes $\beta$ such that $L \cdot \beta < k$ .
In addition, there are no $\mathbb { A } ^ { 1 }$ -classes $\beta$ with $\beta \cdot L = 0$ .

Let $\mathfrak { D }$ be the scattering diagram obtained by reducing $\mathfrak { D } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ modulo $I$ as follows.
For each ray $\mathfrak { o }$ of $\mathfrak { D } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ , we truncate the attached function $f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ by removing monomial terms lying in $I \cdot \Bbbk \lfloor P _ { \varphi _ { \tau _ { 0 } } } \rfloor$ , and we discard the ray if the truncated function equals 1. Because of (II), $\mathfrak { D }$ has only finitely many rays $\mathfrak { o }$ and the attached functions $f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ are finite sums of monomials.
Because of (I), $\mathfrak { D }$ is empty if $I = J$ .

We use the scattering diagram $\mathfrak { D }$ to define a complex analytic space $X _ { I } ^ { o } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ as follows.
Recall from (2.7) the description of the schemes $U _ { \rho _ { i } , I } / S _ { I }$ for $\rho _ { i } \in \Sigma$ :

$$
U _ { \rho _ { i } , I } = V ( X _ { i - 1 } X _ { i + 1 } - z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } X _ { i } ^ { - D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } } f _ { \rho } ) \subset \mathbb { A } _ { X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i + 1 } } ^ { 2 } \times ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { i } } \times S _ { I } .
$$

We have open subsets $U _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i - 1 , i } , I } , U _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } \subset U _ { \rho _ { i } , I }$ defined by $X _ { i - 1 } \neq 0$ and $X _ { i + 1 } \neq 0$ respectively.
We have canonical identifications

$$
U _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } = U _ { \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } = U _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I }
$$

where

$$
U _ { \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } } = ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { i } , X _ { i + 1 } } ^ { 2 } \times S _ { I } .
$$

Recall that we have an open covering $\textstyle X _ { J } ^ { o } = \bigcup _ { \rho \in \Sigma } V _ { \rho , J }$ and open analytic embeddings $V _ { \rho , J } \subset U _ { \rho , J }$ .
Write

$$
\begin{array} { r } { V _ { \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } : = ( V _ { \rho _ { i } , J } \cap U _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } ) \cap ( V _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , J } \cap U _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } ) \subset U _ { \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } } \end{array}
$$

where we use the identification (7.3).
Let $V _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } ~ \subset ~ V _ { \rho _ { i } , J }$ , $V _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J } ~ \subset ~ V _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , J }$ denote the open subsets corresponding to $V _ { \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , J }$ under (7.3).
Let $V _ { \rho _ { i } , I }$ , $V _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I }$ , etc., be the infinitesimal thickenings of these open sets determined by the thickenings $U _ { \rho _ { i } , I }$ of $U _ { \rho _ { i } , J }$ .
Let $\theta _ { \gamma , \mathfrak { D } } \colon U _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } \to U _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I }$ be the gluing isomorphism defined as in §2.2.
Note that as the canonical scattering diagram $\mathfrak { D } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ is trivial modulo $J$ , $\theta _ { \gamma , \mathfrak { D } }$ restricts to the identification (7.3) modulo $J$ , and thus restricts to an isomorphism

$$
V _ { \rho _ { i + 1 } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } \to V _ { \rho _ { i } , \sigma _ { i , i + 1 } , I } .
$$

Gluing the $V _ { \rho , I }$ via these isomorphisms we obtain an infinitesimal deformation $X _ { I } ^ { o } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ of $X _ { J } ^ { o } / S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ .
Note that there are no triple overlaps of the $V _ { \rho , J }$ by Theorem 7.5(2)(b), hence no compatibility condition for the gluing automorphisms.
It is clear from the construction that the families $X _ { I } ^ { o } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ and $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ are compatible.

We define sections $\vartheta _ { q } \in \Gamma ( X _ { I } ^ { o } , { \mathcal { O } } _ { X _ { I } ^ { o } } )$ for $q \in B ( \mathbb { Z } )$ , compatible with the sections of Theorem 2.28, (2).
We proceed as in the algebraic case: we first define a local section Lift $_ Q ( q )$ for each choice of basepoint $Q \in B _ { 0 } \setminus \mathrm { S u p p } ( \mathfrak { D } )$ on a corresponding open patch of $X _ { I } ^ { o }$ using the broken lines construction.
The new difficulty here is that the functions Lift $_ Q ( q )$ are not algebraic, even over the unthickened locus $S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ .
Indeed, by definition ${ \mathrm { L i f t } } _ { Q } ( q ) = \sum { \mathrm { M o n o } } ( \gamma )$ is a formal sum of monomials corresponding to broken lines $\gamma$ for $q$ with endpoint $Q$ .
Note that with our current choice of ideal $J$ , this sum is always infinite, as is already evident in Example 2.18. So we must prove convergence.
This is done in §7.3.1, see Propositions 7.10 and 7.11.

Once this convergence is proved, we observe that these patch to give well-defined global sections.
This follows from the consistency of $\mathfrak { D } ^ { \mathrm { c a n } }$ and compatibility of $X _ { I } ^ { o } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ with $X _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } } ^ { o } / S _ { \mathfrak { m } ^ { N + 1 } }$ for $N \geq 0$ .

We define an infinitesimal thickening $X _ { I } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ of $X _ { J } / S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ by $\mathcal { O } _ { X _ { I } } ~ = ~ i _ { * } \mathcal { O } _ { X _ { I } ^ { o } }$ where $i \colon X _ { J } ^ { o } \subset X _ { J }$ is the inclusion.
Then $X _ { I } / S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ is flat by Lemma 2.29 and the existence of the lifts $\vartheta _ { q }$ .


7.3.1. Convergence of Lifts.
Let $\overline { { C } } \subset M _ { \mathbb { R } }$ be the closure of the support $| \tilde { \Sigma } |$ of the fan $\dot { \Sigma }$ , a closed convex cone.
Let $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ be generators of $\overline { { C } }$ .
Then $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ are eigenvectors of $T$ with eigenvalues $\lambda ^ { - 1 } , \lambda$ for some $\lambda \in \mathbb { R }$ .
We may assume that $\lambda > 1$ .
Let $\pi \colon \bar { B } _ { 0 }  B _ { 0 }$ denote the universal cover of $B _ { 0 }$ .
So $\tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ is identified with $C = \operatorname { I n t } ( { \overline { { C } } } )$ , with deck transformations given by the action of $\Gamma = \langle T \rangle$ on $C$ .
Let $\tilde { \mathcal P }$ , $\tilde { \varphi }$ , and $\tilde { B } _ { 0 } ( \mathbb { Z } )$ denote the pullbacks of $\mathcal { P }$ , $\varphi$ , and $B _ { 0 } ( \mathbb { Z } )$ .
Let $\mathfrak { D }$ denote the scattering diagram on $\ddot { B } _ { 0 }$ induced by $\mathfrak { D }$ .
We fix a trivialization of $\tilde { \mathcal P }$ as the constant sheaf with fibre $P ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \oplus M$ .

The behaviour of the broken lines $\gamma$ is best studied by passing to the universal cover ${ \tilde { B } } _ { 0 }$ of $B _ { 0 }$ .
Let $Q \in B _ { 0 }$ , $q \in B _ { 0 } ( \mathbb { Z } )$ , and choose lifts $\tilde { Q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ , $\tilde { q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 } ( \mathbb { Z } )$ .
Then a broken line $\gamma$ on $B _ { 0 }$ for $q$ with endpoint $Q$ lifts uniquely to a broken line $\tilde { \gamma }$ on $\tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ , for some $N \in \mathbb { Z }$ , and the attached monomials are identified via $\tilde { \mathcal { P } } = \pi ^ { * } \mathcal { P }$ .
Note that $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ approaches $\mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \cdot w _ { 2 }$ as $N  \infty$ and $\mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \cdot w _ { 1 }$ as $N \to - \infty$ .

If $\gamma$ is a broken line for a point $\tilde { q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 } ( \mathbb { Z } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ then $\gamma \colon ( - \infty , 0 ] $ ${ \tilde { B } } _ { 0 }$ is a piecewise linear path in $\tilde { B } _ { 0 } = C$ with initial direction $- \bar { q }$ , ending at $\tilde { Q }$ , and crossing all the rays of $\tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ between $\mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \tilde { q }$ and $\mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \tilde { Q }$ in order.
Let $t _ { 1 } , \ldots , t _ { l } \in ( - \infty , 0 )$ denote the points where $\gamma$ is not affine linear.
Each point $\gamma ( t _ { i } )$ lies on a ray $\boldsymbol { 0 } _ { i }$ of $\mathfrak { D }$ and the change $\gamma ^ { \prime } ( t _ { i } + \epsilon ) - \gamma ^ { \prime } ( t _ { i } - \epsilon )$ in the direction of $\gamma$ as it crosses $\boldsymbol { \mathsf { o } } _ { i }$ is an integral multiple of the primitive generator of $\boldsymbol { 0 } _ { i }$ .
Moreover this multiple is positive because each ray of the canonical scattering diagram is an outgoing ray in the terminology of Definition 2.13. So the path $\gamma$ is “convex when viewed from the origin”.

It is convenient for the convergence calculation to decompose the monomials for broken lines as follows.
Let $\gamma \colon ( - \infty , 0 ]  \dot { B } _ { 0 }$ be a broken line, $t \in ( - \infty , 0 ]$ a point such that $\gamma$ is affine linear near $t$ and $\gamma ( t )$ lies in the interior of a maximal cone $\sigma$ o f $\tilde { \Sigma }$ , and $c { z } ^ { q }$ the monomial attached to the domain of linearity of $\gamma$ containing $t$ .
Here $c \in \Bbbk$ and $q \in  { \mathcal { P } } _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } } \subset  { \mathcal { P } } ^ { \mathrm { g p } } \oplus M$ .
We write $c z ^ { q } = a z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } ( m ) }$ , where $m = r ( q ) \in M$ and $a = c z ^ { q - \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } ( m ) }$ is a monomial in $\mathbb { k } \lfloor P \rfloor$ .
We also use the same decomposition for the monomials occuring in the scattering functions $f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ for $\mathfrak { d } \in \tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ .
Let $\mathfrak { d }$ be a ray in $\tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ with primitive integral generator $m \in M$ and $\tau = \tau _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ the smallest cone of $\tilde { \Sigma }$ containing $\mathfrak { o }$ .
Then $f _ { \mathfrak { d } } - 1$ is a sum of monomials $c z ^ { q }$ where $c \in \mathbb { k }$ and $q \in P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau } }$ , $0 \neq - r ( q ) \in \mathfrak { d }$ .
We write $c z ^ { q } = a z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau } ( m ) }$ where $m = r ( q )$ and $\begin{array} { r } { a = c z ^ { q - \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau } ( m ) } } \end{array}$ is a monomial in $\mathbb { k } [ P ]$ .

The scattering diagram $\mathfrak { D }$ on $B$ is finite (because we have reduced modulo $I$ ), and $\tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ is its inverse image under $\pi \colon \tilde { B } _ { 0 }  B _ { 0 }$ .
Thus $\tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ has only finitely many $\Gamma$ -orbits of rays.
Moreover, the $\Gamma$ -action on the scattering functions $f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ is induced by the given action on $M _ { \mathbb { R } }$ and the trivial action on $\mathbb { k } \lfloor P \rfloor$ as follows: writing $\begin{array} { r } { f _ { \mathfrak { d } } = 1 + \sum a _ { m } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau } ( m ) } } \end{array}$ as above, $\begin{array} { r } { f _ { T ( 0 ) } = 1 + \sum a _ { m } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { T ( \tau ) } ( T ( m ) ) } } \end{array}$ .

Lemma 7.8. Let $\tilde { Q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 } \setminus \mathrm { S u p p } ( \tilde { \mathfrak { D } } )$ be a point contained in the interior of a maximal cone $\sigma \in \dot { \Sigma }$ .
We consider broken lines $\gamma$ on $\tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ , some $N \in \mathbb { Z }$ , with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ , such that $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) \notin I \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } } ]$ .
Let $k \geq 0$ be such that $( k + 1 ) J \subset I$ .

(1) The number of bends of $\gamma$ is at most $k$ .  
(2) The number of broken lines for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ is $O ( | N | ^ { k } )$ .

(3) For $\gamma$ a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ write $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } ( m _ { \gamma } ) }$ where $a _ { \gamma }$ is a monomial in $\mathbb { k } [ P ]$ .
Assume that $| z ^ { p } | < \epsilon < 1$ for all $p \in P$ .
Then

$$
\vert a _ { \gamma } \vert = O ( \prod _ { \stackrel { \rho \in \Sigma } { \dim \rho = 1 } } \vert z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } \vert ^ { \vert N \vert } ) .
$$

Proof.
(1) At a bend $t _ { i } \in ( - \infty , 0 ]$ of $\gamma$ the attached monomial $c _ { i } z ^ { q _ { i } }$ is replaced by the monomial $c _ { i + 1 } z ^ { q _ { i + 1 } } = c z ^ { q } \cdot c _ { i } z ^ { q _ { i } }$ where $c z ^ { q }$ is a term in a positive power of the scattering function $f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ associated to the ray $\mathfrak { o }$ containing $\gamma ( t _ { i } )$ .
In particular $c z ^ { q } \in J \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau _ { \mathfrak { d } } } } ]$ .
Since $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) \notin I \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } } ]$ and $( k + 1 ) J \subset I$ it follows that there are at most $k$ bends.

(2) Such a broken line crosses $O ( | N | )$ scattering rays.
If $\gamma$ is a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ then the initial attached monomial is specified, equal to $z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } ( T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) ) }$ .
At a scattering ray $\mathfrak { o }$ , let $u$ denote the primitive generator of $\mathfrak { o }$ , $f \ = \ f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ the attached function, and let $c z ^ { q }$ be the monomial attached to the incoming segment of the broken line.
Then the possible continuations of the broken line past $\mathfrak { o }$ correspond to the monomial terms in $f ^ { d }$ , where $d = | r ( q ) \land u |$ is the index of the sublattice of $M$ generated by $r ( q )$ and $u$ .
Note that since $f \equiv 1 \mod J \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau _ { 0 } } } ]$ the number of monomial terms in $f ^ { d }$ not lying in $I \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau _ { 0 } } } ]$ is bounded independent of $d$ .
Further, since there are a finite number of $\Gamma$ -orbits of scattering rays, and the $\Gamma$ -action preserves monomials, there is a bound on the number of monomial terms independent of the ray $\mathfrak { o }$ .
Thus for a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ there ar e O(|N|)k ! = O(|N|k) choices of how it may bend by (1).
So the total number of broken lines is $O ( | N | ^ { k } )$ .

(3) By symmetry we may assume that $N \geq 0$ .
Let $\mathfrak { d } \in \tilde { \mathfrak { D } }$ be a scattering ray, $f = f _ { 0 }$ the attached function, and $\gamma$ a broken line that crosses $\mathfrak { o }$ .
Suppose first that $\mathfrak { o }$ is contained in the interior of a maximal cone $\sigma$ of $\tilde { \Sigma }$ .
Let $a z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } ( m ) }$ be the monomial attached to the incoming segment of $\gamma$ near $\mathfrak { o }$ .
Let $u$ be the primitive generator of $\mathfrak { o }$ .
Then the outgoing monomial $a ^ { \prime } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma } ( m ^ { \prime } ) }$ is obtained from the incoming monomial by multiplication by a monomial term in $f ^ { d }$ , where $d = | m \land u |$ .
Write $f = 1 + f _ { 1 } + \cdot \cdot \cdot + f _ { r }$ , a sum of monomials.
Since $f \equiv 1 \mod J \cdot \Bbbk [ P _ { \varphi \sigma } ]$ we have

$$
f ^ { d } \equiv \sum _ { i _ { 1 } + \cdots + i _ { r } \leq k } \binom { d } { i _ { 1 } , \ldots , i _ { r } } f _ { 1 } ^ { i _ { 1 } } \cdot \cdot \cdot f _ { r } ^ { i _ { r } } \mod I \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \varphi _ { \sigma } } ] .
$$

The multinomial coefficient

$$
{ \binom { d } { i _ { 1 } , \dots , i _ { r } } } : = { \frac { d ! } { i _ { 1 } ! \cdot \cdot \cdot i _ { r } ! ( d - i _ { 1 } - \cdot \cdot \cdot - i _ { r } ) ! } }
$$

is bounded by $d ^ { k }$ .
The direction of the scattering ray $\mathfrak { o }$ is $u = T ^ { s } ( \beta )$ where $0 \leq s \leq N$ and $\beta \in M$ is chosen from a finite set.

The vector $m \in M$ is of the form

$$
m = T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) - \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { l } T ^ { s _ { i } } \alpha _ { i }
$$

where $l \ \leq \ k$ , $0 \leq s _ { i } \leq N$ for each $i$ , and the $\alpha _ { i } \in M$ are chosen from a finite set.
Indeed, as in the proof of (2), for the monomial terms $c { z } ^ { q }$ occurring in the powers $f ^ { d }$ of the function $f = f _ { \mathfrak { d } }$ attached to a given scattering ray $\mathfrak { d }$ , only finitely many exponents $q \in P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau _ { \mathfrak { d } } } }$ occur (working modulo $I \cdot \mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tau _ { 0 } } } ]$ ).
So there are only finitely many possible changes of exponent $q$ for the attached monomial $c { z } ^ { q }$ of a broken line at a scattering ray modulo the action of $\Gamma$ .

Now identify $M = \mathbb { Z } ^ { 2 }$ and let $\| \cdot \|$ denote the standard norm on $M _ { \mathbb { R } } = \mathbb { R } ^ { 2 }$ .
Then

$$
d = | m \wedge u | \leq \| m \| \cdot \| u \| = O ( \lambda ^ { 2 N } ) .
$$

So, the coefficient $a ^ { \prime } \in \mathbb { k } | P |$ of the outgoing monomial is given by $a ^ { \prime } = c \cdot z ^ { p } \cdot a$ where $c \in \mathbb { C }$ , $p \in { \cal P }$ , and $| c | = O ( \lambda ^ { 2 k N } )$ .
Thus $| a ^ { \prime } | = O ( \lambda ^ { 2 k N } ) \cdot | a |$ for $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ .

Next, let $\boldsymbol { \rho } \in \tilde { \Sigma }$ be a ray and $\sigma _ { + }$ , $\sigma _ { - }$ the maximal cones containing $\rho$ .
Suppose $\gamma$ is a broken line that crosses $\rho$ , travelling from $\sigma _ { - }$ to $o _ { + }$ .
Let $a _ { - } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } \sigma _ { - } ( m ) }$ be the monomial attached to the incoming segment of $\gamma$ near $\rho$ and $a _ { + } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma _ { + } } ( m ^ { \prime } ) }$ the monomial attached to the outgoing segment.
By the definition of $\tilde { \varphi }$ ,

$$
z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma _ { - } } ( m ) } = ( z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } ) ^ { - \langle n _ { \rho } , m \rangle } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma _ { + } } ( m ) } ,
$$

where $n _ { \rho } \in N$ is primitive, annihilates $\rho$ , and is positive on $\sigma _ { + }$ .
Write $d : = - \langle n _ { \rho } , m \rangle$ ; note $d = | u \land m | > 0$ where $u \in M$ is the primitive generator of $\rho$ .
If $\gamma$ does not bend at $\rho$ then $a _ { + } = ( z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } ) ^ { d } \cdot a _ { - }$ .
In general $a _ { + } = ( z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } ) ^ { d } \cdot a _ { - } ^ { \prime }$ where $a _ { - } ^ { \prime } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma _ { - } } ( m ^ { \prime } ) }$ is obtained from $a _ { - } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \sigma _ { - } } ( m ) }$ as above (by applying the scattering automorphism associated to $\rho$ and selecting a monomial term).

We need to show the exponent $d = | u \land m | > 0$ of $z ^ { \left\lfloor D _ { \rho } \right\rfloor }$ in the previous paragraph is large for some lift $\tilde { \rho }$ of any given ray $\rho \in \Sigma$ .
This will allow us to absorb the $O ( \lambda ^ { 2 N } )$ factors coming from bends of $\gamma$ and obtain the estimate (3).
Let $\gamma$ be a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ .
Then

$$
m _ { \gamma } = T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) - \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { l } T ^ { s _ { i } } \alpha _ { i }
$$

as above, where $0 \leq l \leq k$ , $N \geq s _ { 1 } \geq \cdot \cdot \cdot \geq s _ { l } \geq 0$ , and the $\alpha _ { i }$ lie in a finite set.
Write $s _ { 0 } = N$ and $s _ { l + 1 } = 0$ .
Choose $j$ such that $s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } \geq N / ( k + 1 )$ .
Now consider the exponent $d = | u \land m |$ for $\begin{array} { r } { m = T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) - \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { j } T ^ { s _ { i } } \alpha _ { i } } \end{array}$ given by the monomial attached to the segment of the broken line between bends $j$ and $j + 1$ .
Let $\tilde { \rho } \in \tilde { \Sigma }$ be the lift of $\rho \in \Sigma$ between bends $j$ and $j + 1$ which is closest to bend $j + 1$ (such a lift exists if $N$ is sufficiently large).
Let $u \ : = \ : T ^ { s _ { j + 1 } } \beta$ be the primitive generator of $\tilde { \rho }$ .
Then $| u \land m | = | \beta \land T ^ { s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } } m ^ { \prime } |$ where $m ^ { \prime } = T ^ { - s _ { j } } ( m )$ .
Writing $m \prime = \mu _ { 1 } ^ { \prime } w _ { 1 } + \mu _ { 2 } ^ { \prime } w _ { 2 }$ , we see that $| \mu _ { 1 } ^ { \prime } |$ is bounded since $w _ { 1 }$ has eigenvalue $\lambda ^ { - 1 } < 1$ .
Also, $\mu _ { 2 } ^ { \prime }$ is bounded away from zero by Lemma 7.9. Now

$$
u \wedge m = \beta \wedge T ^ { s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } } m ^ { \prime } = \mu _ { 1 } ^ { \prime } ( \beta \wedge w _ { 1 } ) \lambda ^ { - ( s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } ) } + \mu _ { 2 } ^ { \prime } ( \beta \wedge w _ { 2 } ) \lambda ^ { s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } } ,
$$

where $s _ { j } - s _ { j + 1 } > N / ( k + 1 )$ , so

$$
| u \land m | > c \cdot \lambda ^ { N / ( k + 1 ) }
$$

for some constant $c > 0$ .

Combining our results now gives, when $| z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } | < 1$ for all $p \in P _ { \mathrm { b d y } }$ , the estimate

$$
a _ { \gamma } = O ( ( \lambda ^ { 2 k N } ) ^ { k } \cdot \prod _ { \stackrel { \rho \in \Sigma } { \dim \rho = 1 } } | z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } | ^ { c \cdot \lambda ^ { N / ( k + 1 ) } } ) .
$$

where the first factor bounds the contribution associated to bends of $\gamma$ and the second factor bounds the contribution associated to rays $\rho$ of the fan crossed by $\gamma$ , as described in the preceding two paragraphs.
This implies the estimate (3) in the statement, using $| z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } | < 1$ .
Indeed, the above expression is of the form

$$
\lambda ^ { a N } \cdot x ^ { c \cdot \lambda ^ { b N } }
$$

where $a , b , c > 0$ and $\lambda > 1$ are constants, and $x = \prod \left. z ^ { \lfloor D _ { \rho } \rfloor } \right.$ .
This is bounded by $C x ^ { N }$ for $0 \leq x < \epsilon < 1$ , for some constant $C$ (depending on $\epsilon$ ).
(To see this, we may assume $x \neq 0$ , take logarithms, and establish an inequality

$$
a N \log \lambda + c \lambda ^ { b N } \log x \leq \log C + N \log x
$$

We have $- \log x > - \log \epsilon > 0$ .
Rearranging (7.5), we require that, for some choice of $C$ ,

$$
a N \log \lambda \le \log C + ( - \log x ) ( c \lambda ^ { b N } - N )
$$

for all $N$ .
This holds because

$$
a N \log \lambda \le ( - \log x ) ( c \lambda ^ { b N } - N )
$$

for $N$ sufficiently large.)

Lemma 7.9. Let $A \subset \mathbb { R }$ be a finite set and $\lambda \in \mathbb { R }$ , $\lambda > 1$ .
For $k \in \mathbb N$ let $S _ { k } \subset \mathbb { R }$ be the set of real numbers s of the form $\textstyle s = \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { l } c _ { i } \lambda ^ { n _ { i } }$ where $l \leq k$ and $c _ { i } \in A$ , $n _ { i } \in \mathbb { Z } _ { \geq 0 }$ for each $i$ .
Then $S _ { k }$ is discrete for each $k$ .

Proof.
Proof by induction on $k$ .
We have $S _ { 0 } = \{ 0 \}$ .
Suppose $S _ { k }$ is discrete.
We have $\textstyle S _ { k + 1 } = \bigcup _ { n \geq 0 } \lambda ^ { n } ( S _ { k } + A )$ .
Since $\lambda > 1$ we deduce that $S _ { k + 1 }$ discrete.


For Propositions 7.10 and 7.11 below, the assertions hold after possibly replacing $X _ { J }$ by a smaller neighbourhood of $s ( 0 ) \in X _ { J }$ (independent of $I$ , $Q$ and $q$ ).

Proposition 7.10. Let $Q \in B _ { 0 } \setminus \mathrm { S u p p } ( \mathfrak { D } )$ be a point contained in the interior of a maximal cone $O$ of $\Sigma$ .
Each term of the formal sum $\mathrm { L i f t } _ { Q } ( q ) = \sum \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) $ is an analytic function on $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ and the sum defines an analytic function on $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ .

Proof.
Recall that $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ is an infinitesimal thickening of the reduced complex analytic space $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , J }$ .
Write

$$
V _ { \sigma , \sigma } : = \{ ( X _ { 1 } , X _ { 2 } ) | | X _ { 1 } | < R | X _ { 2 } | , | X _ { 2 } | < R | X _ { 1 } | \} \subset ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { 1 } , X _ { 2 } } ^ { 2 } \times S .
$$

Then $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ is a reduced complex analytic space containing $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ as a locally closed subspace.
We show that the sum Lift $_ Q ( q )$ converges (uniformly on compact sets) to an analytic function on a neighbourhood of $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ in $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ .

Let $\tilde { Q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ be a lift of $Q$ and $\tilde { \sigma }$ the lift of $\sigma$ containing $\tilde { Q }$ .
Let $u _ { 1 } , u _ { 2 }$ be the primitive generators of $\tilde { \sigma }$ (a basis of $M$ ) such that the orientation of $u _ { 1 } , u _ { 2 }$ agrees with that of $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ .
Let $X _ { i } = z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( u _ { i } ) }$ , $i = 1 , 2$ , be the associated coordinate functions on $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I }$ , so that

$$
V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I } \subset \{ ( X _ { 1 } , X _ { 2 } ) \mid | X _ { 1 } | < R | X _ { 2 } | , | X _ { 2 } | < R | X _ { 1 } | \} \subset ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { 1 } , X _ { 2 } } ^ { 2 } \times S _ { I } ^ { \prime } .
$$

For $m \in M$ , writing $m = \alpha _ { 1 } u _ { 1 } + \alpha _ { 2 } u _ { 2 }$ , we have $z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m ) } = X _ { 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { 1 } } X _ { 2 } ^ { \alpha _ { 2 } }$ .

As already noted, broken lines $\gamma$ on $B _ { 0 }$ for $q$ with endpoint $Q$ lift uniquely to broken lines on $\tilde { B } _ { 0 }$ for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ , for some $N \in \mathbb { Z }$ , and the attached monomials are identified.
Write $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) }$ and $m _ { \gamma } = \alpha _ { 1 } u _ { 1 } + \alpha _ { 2 } u _ { 2 }$ .
Clearly $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } X _ { 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { 1 } } X _ { 2 } ^ { \alpha _ { 2 } } \in \mathbb { k } [ P ] [ X _ { 1 } ^ { \pm 1 } , X _ { 2 } ^ { \pm 1 } ]$ is an analytic function on $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ .
Also write $m _ { \gamma } = \mu _ { 1 } w _ { 1 } + \mu _ { 2 } w _ { 2 }$ .
By Lemma 7.12, (1), $\mu _ { 1 }$ and $\mu _ { 2 }$ are bounded below (using the symmetric statement interchanging $w _ { 1 }$ and $w _ { 2 }$ if $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) \in \langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 1 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } } )$ .
The points $u _ { 1 }$ and $u _ { 2 }$ are adjacent integral points on the boundary of the infinite convex polytope $\Xi$ with asymptotic directions $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ .
It follows that $w _ { 1 } = \beta _ { 1 } u _ { 2 } + \gamma _ { 1 } ( u _ { 1 } - u _ { 2 } )$ and $w _ { 2 } = \beta _ { 2 } u _ { 1 } + \gamma _ { 2 } ( u _ { 2 } - u _ { 1 } )$ , for some $\beta _ { 1 } , \beta _ { 2 } , \gamma _ { 1 } , \gamma _ { 2 } > 0$ .
Hence

$$
| z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } \tilde { \sigma } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } | = | X _ { 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { 1 } } X _ { 2 } ^ { \alpha _ { 2 } } | = ( | X _ { 2 } | ^ { \beta _ { 1 } } | X _ { 1 } / X _ { 2 } | ^ { \gamma _ { 1 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 1 } } ( | X _ { 1 } | ^ { \beta _ { 2 } } | X _ { 2 } / X _ { 1 } | ^ { \gamma _ { 2 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 2 } } .
$$

Now $| X _ { 1 } / X _ { 2 } | < R$ , $| X _ { 2 } / X _ { 1 } | < R$ on $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ .
Thus, as we have chosen $\delta$ in Lemma 7.6 so that $0 < \delta < \operatorname* { m i n } ( R ^ { - \gamma _ { 1 } / \beta _ { 1 } } , R ^ { - \gamma _ { 2 } / \beta _ { 2 } } )$ , if $\mu _ { 1 } , \mu _ { 2 }$ are both positive, $\big | z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } \big |$ is bounded for $| X _ { 1 } | , | X _ { 2 } | < \delta$ .
On the other hand, suppose $\mu _ { 1 }$ , say, is negative.
Then if $| X _ { 2 } | > \delta ^ { \prime } > 0$ , we have

$$
( | X _ { 2 } | ^ { \beta _ { 1 } } | X _ { 1 } / X _ { 2 } | ^ { \gamma _ { 1 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 1 } } < ( \delta ^ { \prime } ) ^ { \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } | X _ { 2 } / X _ { 1 } | ^ { - \mu _ { 1 } \gamma _ { 1 } } < ( \delta ^ { \prime } ) ^ { \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } R ^ { - \mu _ { 1 } \gamma _ { 1 } } .
$$

Since $\beta _ { 1 }$ and $\gamma _ { 1 }$ are fixed and $\mu _ { 1 }$ is bounded below, the above quantity is bounded.
Similarly, if $\mu _ { 2 }$ is negative, $( | X _ { 1 } | ^ { \beta _ { 2 } } | X _ { 2 } / X _ { 1 } | ^ { \gamma _ { 2 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 2 } }$ is bounded provided $| X _ { 1 } | > \delta ^ { \prime } > 0$ .
Thus in any event, $| z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } |$ is bounded for $0 < \delta ^ { \prime } < | X _ { 1 } | , | X _ { 2 } | < \delta$ .
(We will only obtain uniform convergence of the series $\operatorname { L i f t } _ { Q } ( q )$ on compact subsets of $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ .) By Lemma 7.8, (3), if $| z ^ { p } | < \epsilon < 1$ for all $p \in { \cal P }$ we have $| a _ { \gamma } | = O ( \epsilon ^ { | N | } )$ .
By Lemma 7.8, (2), the number of broken lines for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ is $O ( | N | ^ { k } )$ .
Combining, we deduce that ${ \mathrm { L i f t } } _ { q } ( Q ) = \sum { \mathrm { M o n o } } ( \gamma )$ is convergent on the open analytic subset $V _ { \sigma , \sigma } ^ { \prime }$ of $V _ { \sigma , \sigma }$ defined by $| X _ { 1 } | , | X _ { 2 } | < \delta$ and $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ for all $p \in { \cal P }$ , for some $\delta > 0$ (independent of $I$ and $q$ ).
After replacing $X _ { J }$ by an analytic neighbourhood of the vertex $s ( 0 ) \in X _ { J }$ , we may assume that $V _ { \sigma , \sigma , I } \subset V _ { \sigma , \sigma } ^ { \prime }$ .


Proposition 7.11. Let $Q \in B _ { 0 } \setminus \mathrm { S u p p } ( \mathfrak { D } )$ be a point contained in the interior of a maximal cone $\sigma$ of $\Sigma$ and let $\rho$ be an edge of $\sigma$ .
Consider the formal sum L $\operatorname { i f t } _ { Q } ( q ) =$ $\textstyle \sum \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ .
For $Q$ sufficiently close to $\rho$ each term of the sum is an analytic function on $V _ { \rho , I }$ and the sum defines an analytic function on $V _ { \rho , I }$ .

Proof.
Write $\rho = \rho _ { i }$ , without loss of generality assume $\sigma = \sigma _ { i , i + 1 }$ , so that $\sigma _ { i - 1 , i } \in \Sigma$ is the other maximal cone containing $\rho _ { i }$ .
Let $\tilde { Q } , \tilde { \rho } _ { i } , \tilde { \sigma } _ { i , i + 1 } , \tilde { \sigma } _ { i - 1 , i }$ be compatible lifts to $\ddot { B } _ { 0 }$ .
Let $u _ { i } , u _ { i - 1 } , u _ { i + 1 }$ be the primitive generators of $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ and the remaining edges of $\tilde { \sigma } _ { i - 1 , i }$ and $\tilde { \sigma } _ { i , i + 1 }$ , and write $X _ { i } , X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i + 1 }$ for the corresponding coordinates on $V _ { \rho , I }$ .
So

$$
\begin{array} { r } { ( X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i } , X _ { i + 1 } ) \mid | ~ X _ { i - 1 } | < R | X _ { i } | , | X _ { i + 1 } | < R | X _ { i } | \} \subset V ( X _ { i - 1 } X _ { i + 1 } - z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } X _ { i } ^ { - D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } } f _ { i } ^ { - 1 } ) \mid | ~ Y _ { i - 1 }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i - 1 }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i - 1 }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i - 1 }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  \mid | ~ Y _ { i }  , } \\ { \subset \mathbb { A } _ { X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i + 1 } } ^ { 2 } \times ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { i } } \times S _ { I } ^ { \prime } . } \end{array}
$$

Define

$$
\begin{array} { r l } & { X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i } , X _ { i + 1 } ) \mid | X _ { i - 1 } | < R | X _ { i } | , | X _ { i + 1 } | < R | X _ { i } | \} \subset V ( X _ { i - 1 } X _ { i + 1 } - z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } X _ { i } ^ { - D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } } f _ { \rho , i } } \\ & { \qquad \subset \mathbb { A } _ { X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i + 1 } } ^ { 2 } \times ( \mathbb { G } _ { m } ) _ { X _ { i } } \times S . } \end{array}
$$

We assume that the orientation of $u _ { i - 1 } , u _ { i + 1 }$ is the same as that of $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ .

We first consider broken lines $\gamma$ lying in the cone generated by $u _ { i }$ and $w _ { 2 }$ .
Write $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } _ { i , i + 1 } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) }$ , and $m _ { \gamma } = \alpha u _ { i } + \alpha _ { + } u _ { i + 1 } = \mu _ { 1 } w _ { 1 } + \mu _ { 2 } w _ { 2 }$ .
By Lemma 7.12,(1), $| \mu _ { 1 } |$ is bounded, and $\mu _ { 2 } > 0$ for all but finitely many $\gamma$ .
By Lemma 7.12,(2), $\alpha _ { + } \geq 0$ , so $\begin{array} { r } { \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha } X _ { i + 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { + } } \in \mathbb { k } [ P ] [ X _ { i } ^ { \pm 1 } , X _ { i - 1 } , X _ { i + 1 } ] } \end{array}$ is analytic on $V _ { \rho }$ for each $\gamma$ .
In particular we may assume in what follows (discarding finitely many terms $\operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ ) that $\mu _ { 2 } > 0$ .
Writing $w _ { 1 } = - \beta _ { 1 } u _ { i + 1 } + \gamma _ { 1 } u _ { i }$ and $w _ { 2 } = \beta _ { 2 } u _ { i } + \gamma _ { 2 } ( u _ { i + 1 } - u _ { i } )$ , we have $\beta _ { 1 } , \beta _ { 2 } , \gamma _ { 1 } , \gamma _ { 2 } > 0$ and

$$
| z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } \tilde { \sigma } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } | = ( | X _ { i + 1 } | ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } } | X _ { i } | ^ { \gamma _ { 1 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 1 } } ( | X _ { i } | ^ { \beta _ { 2 } } | X _ { i + 1 } / X _ { i } | ^ { \gamma _ { 2 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 2 } } .
$$

Recall that $| X _ { i + 1 } / X _ { i } | , | X _ { i - 1 } / X _ { i } | < R$ on $V _ { \rho }$ .
Note then that for $0 < \delta < R ^ { - \gamma _ { 2 } / \beta _ { 2 } }$ , the second factor on the right is bounded for $| X _ { i } | < \delta$ as we are taking $\mu _ { 2 } > 0$ .
If $\mu _ { 1 } < 0$ , then we have

$$
( | X _ { i + 1 } | ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } } | X _ { i } | ^ { \gamma _ { 1 } } ) ^ { \mu _ { 1 } } < R ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } | X _ { i } | ^ { ( - \beta _ { 1 } + \gamma _ { 1 } ) \mu _ { 1 } }
$$

which is bounded for $\delta ^ { \prime } < | X _ { i } | < \delta$ for any small $\delta ^ { \prime } > 0$ .
Finally, if $\mu _ { 1 } > 0$ , we use the equation for $V _ { \rho }$ , which gives

$$
| X _ { i + 1 } | ^ { - 1 } = | X _ { i - 1 } | \cdot | X _ { i } | ^ { D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } } \cdot | f _ { \rho } | ^ { - 1 } \cdot | z ^ { - [ D _ { \rho } ] } | .
$$

The function $f _ { \rho }$ on $V _ { \rho }$ restricts to the constant function 1 over $S _ { J }$ .
Hence we may impose the condition $| f _ { \rho } | > \delta ^ { \prime }$ for any small $\delta ^ { \prime } > 0$ .
Note that

$$
1 ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } = ( \vert X _ { i - 1 } \vert \vert X _ { i } \vert ^ { D _ { p } ^ { 2 } } \vert f _ { \rho } \vert ^ { - 1 } \vert z ^ { - [ D _ { p } ] } \vert ) ^ { \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } < R ^ { \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } \vert X _ { i } \vert ^ { \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } ( 1 + D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } ) } \vert f _ { \rho } \vert ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } } \vert z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } \vert ^ { - \beta _ { 1 } \mu _ { 1 } }
$$

Thus we see that in any event, if $\delta ^ { \prime } < | X _ { i } | < \delta$ , $| f _ { \rho } | > \delta ^ { \prime }$ and $| z ^ { p } | < \epsilon < 1$ for all $p \in { \cal P }$ , then

$$
| z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } | \cdot | z ^ { [ D _ { \rho } ] } | ^ { c }
$$

is bounded, where $c = \beta _ { 1 } \cdot \operatorname* { s u p } ( \{ \mu _ { 1 } \} , 0 )$ is a constant.
Now by Lemma 7.8, (3), again using $| z ^ { p } | < \epsilon < 1$ for all $p \in P$ , then

$$
| \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma ) | = | a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) } | = O ( \epsilon ^ { | N | } ) .
$$

Recall that the number of broken lines for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ is $O ( | N | ^ { k } )$ (Lemma 7.8, (2)).
We deduce that the sum $\textstyle \sum \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ over broken lines $\gamma$ lying in $\langle u _ { i } , w _ { 2 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ is uniformly convergent on compact sets for $| X _ { i } | < \delta$ , $f _ { \rho } \neq 0$ , and $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ for all $p \in P$ , where $\delta > 0$ is independent of $I$ and $q$ .

Symmetrically, if we choose a basepoint $Q ^ { \prime } \in \sigma _ { i - 1 , i }$ sufficiently close to $\rho$ , we can use the same argument for broken lines lying in $\langle u _ { i } , w _ { 1 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ .
Such a broken line will have $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } X _ { i - 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { - } } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha }$ with $\alpha _ { - } \geq 0$ .
The same argument as above shows that the sum $\textstyle \sum \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ over all such broken lines $\gamma$ is uniformly convergent on compact sets for $| X _ { i } | < \delta$ , $f _ { \rho } \neq 0$ , and $| z ^ { p } | < 1$ for all $p \in P$ , where $\delta > 0$ is again independent of $I$ and $q$ .
However, the statement we are trying to prove involves the lift at $Q$ , not $Q ^ { \prime }$ .
For this purpose, we will omit terms coming from broken lines with $\alpha _ { - } = 0$ from the above sum, as such terms will also arise in the above analysis at $\tilde { Q }$ .

To deal with this issue, note that given such a broken line $\gamma$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ with $\alpha _ { - } > 0$ , we get a finite number of broken lines $\gamma _ { j }$ , $1 \leq j \leq s$ , ending at a point $\tilde { Q } ^ { \prime \prime } \in \tilde { \sigma } _ { i , i + 1 }$ sufficiently close to $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ as follows.
Extend $\gamma$ until it reaches $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ (which can be done since $\alpha _ { - } > 0$ ).
Then applying the automorphism associated to crossing $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ to $\operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ gives $a _ { \gamma } X _ { i - 1 } ^ { \alpha - } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha } f _ { \rho } ^ { \alpha - }$ , which we write as $\textstyle \sum _ { j = 1 } ^ { s } a _ { \gamma _ { j } } X _ { i - 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { - } } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha _ { j } }$ .
The $j ^ { t h }$ monomial in the sum gives a new broken line bending at $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ (unless , in which case we just extend the final line segment of $\gamma$ ), with new attached monomial $a _ { \gamma _ { j } } X _ { i - 1 } ^ { \alpha _ { - } } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha _ { j } } = a _ { \gamma _ { j } } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } \tilde { \sigma } _ { i , i + 1 } ( m _ { \gamma _ { j } } ) }$ .
As long as ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ lies in the cone generated by $\rho _ { i }$ and $- m _ { \gamma _ { j } }$ , by extending or shortening the last line segment of $\gamma _ { j }$ and applying a homothety, one can obtain a broken line $\gamma _ { j }$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ .
Thus for ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ sufficiently close to $\ddot { \rho } _ { i }$ , we obtain broken lines $\gamma _ { 1 } , \dots , \gamma _ { s }$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ .
However, the choice of ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ may depend on $\gamma$ .
To see there is a choice of ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ which works for all $\gamma$ , note that for all but a finite number of $\gamma$ , $m _ { \gamma }$ lies in the half-space $\mathbb { R } _ { \ge 0 } { \cdot } w _ { 1 } { + } \mathbb { R } { \cdot } w _ { 2 }$ by Lemma 7.12, (1).
Further, since $\gamma _ { j }$ bends at $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ , $m _ { \gamma } \in \mathbb { Z } ^ { . } u _ { i } + \mathbb { Z } _ { < 0 } { \cdot } u _ { i + 1 }$ .
Thus $m _ { \gamma } = \beta u _ { i } + \beta _ { + } u _ { i + 1 }$ for $\beta > 0$ , $\beta _ { + } < 0$ , and $m _ { \gamma _ { j } } = ( \beta - l ) u _ { i } + \beta _ { + } u _ { i + 1 }$ for some $l > 0$ with a bound only depending on $f _ { \rho _ { i } }$ mod $I$ .
$\begin{array} { r } { \boldsymbol { \dot { \lambda } } , } \end{array}$ From this it follows that there cannot be a sequence of $\gamma$ and $\gamma _ { j }$ constructed from $\gamma$ as above so that the cones generated by $u _ { i }$ and $- m _ { \gamma _ { j } }$ get smaller and smaller.

Thus we see that taking $\tilde { Q }$ sufficiently close to $\tilde { \rho } _ { i }$ , the broken lines ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ contained in $\langle w _ { 1 } , \tilde { Q } ^ { \prime } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ with $\alpha _ { - } > 0$ give in the above fashion broken lines ending at $\tilde { Q }$ contained in $\langle w _ { 1 } , \tilde { Q } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ , and every such broken line ending at $\tilde { Q }$ clearly arises in this way.
Furthermore, there are no broken lines contained in $\langle w _ { 1 } , \tilde { Q } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ with $\alpha _ { - } = 0$ , and thus all broken lines ending at $\tilde { Q }$ have been accounted for.

Now consider again a broken line $\gamma$ contained in $\langle w _ { 1 } , \tilde { Q } ^ { \prime } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ with $\alpha _ { - } ~ > ~ 0$ .
By construction, $\begin{array} { r } { \sum _ { j = 1 } ^ { s } \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma _ { j } ) = \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) f _ { \rho } ^ { \alpha _ { - } } } \end{array}$ .
We wish to understand the contribution of $\begin{array} { r } { \sum _ { j = 1 } ^ { s } \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma _ { j } ) } \end{array}$ to $\operatorname { L i f t } _ { Q } ( q )$ , and to do so, we write $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma _ { j } )$ in terms of $X _ { i } , X _ { i + 1 }$ using the relation Xi−1Xi+1 = z[Dρ]X−D2ρi i n $\mathbb { k } [ P _ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \rho } } } ]$ (see Proposition 2.5). So we can write

$$
\sum _ { j } \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma _ { j } ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \alpha _ { - } [ D _ { \rho } ] } X _ { i + 1 } ^ { - \alpha _ { - } } X _ { i } ^ { - \alpha _ { - } D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } + \alpha } f _ { \rho } ^ { \alpha _ { - } } .
$$

This defines a (possibly rational) function on $V _ { \rho }$ .
On the other hand, $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) =$ $a _ { \gamma } X _ { i - 1 } ^ { \alpha - } X _ { i } ^ { \alpha }$ defines a holomorphic function on $V _ { \rho }$ , and using the equation

$$
X _ { i - 1 } X _ { i + 1 } = z ^ { [ D _ { \rho ] } } X _ { i } ^ { - D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } } f _ { \rho }
$$

which is satisfied on $V _ { \rho }$ , we have

$$
\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \alpha _ { - } [ D _ { \rho } ] } X _ { i + 1 } ^ { - \alpha _ { - } } X _ { i } ^ { - \alpha _ { - } D _ { \rho } ^ { 2 } + \alpha } f _ { \rho } ^ { \alpha _ { - } }
$$

as a function on $V _ { \rho }$ .
Thus we see that $\operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma )$ and $\textstyle \sum _ { j } \operatorname { M o n o } ( \gamma _ { j } )$ coincide as functions on $V _ { \rho }$ , in the above interpretation.
(Essentially we are just using the fact that the relation (7.6) encodes the automorphism associated to crossing $\rho$ ).
Thus the fact that $\begin{array} { r } { \sum _ { \gamma } \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) } \end{array}$ defines an analytic function on $V _ { \rho , I }$ for broken lines $\gamma$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ contained in $\langle u _ { i } , w _ { 1 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ implies that the sum $\begin{array} { r } { \sum _ { \gamma } \mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) } \end{array}$ over all broken lines $\gamma$ ending at $\ddot { Q }$ and contained in $\langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 1 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ is analytic.
This implies $\operatorname { L i f t } _ { Q } ( q )$ is analytic on $V _ { \rho , I }$ .


Lemma 7.12. Let $\tilde { Q } \in \tilde { B } _ { 0 } \setminus \mathrm { S u p p } ( \tilde { \mathfrak { D } } )$ be a point contained in the interior of a maximal cone $\tilde { \sigma } \in \tilde { \Sigma }$ .
Consider broken lines $\gamma$ on ${ \tilde { B } } _ { 0 }$ for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ , for all $N \in \mathbb { Z }$ such that $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) \in \langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 2 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ .
Write $\mathrm { M o n o } ( \gamma ) = a _ { \gamma } z ^ { \tilde { \varphi } _ { \tilde { \sigma } } ( m _ { \gamma } ) }$ , and $m _ { \gamma } = \mu _ { 1 } w _ { 1 } + \mu _ { 2 } w _ { 2 }$ .

(1) $| \mu _ { 1 } |$ is bounded, and $\mu _ { 2 }$ is positive for all but finitely many $\gamma$ .
In particular, $\mu _ { 1 } , \mu _ { 2 }$ are bounded below.

(2) Let $u _ { 1 } , u _ { 2 }$ be generators of $\tilde { \sigma }$ with the same orientation as $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ .
Then for $\ddot { Q }$ sufficiently close to $\tilde { \rho } : = \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \cdot u _ { 1 }$ , $m _ { \gamma }$ lies in the half space $\mathbb { R } \cdot u _ { 1 } + \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } \cdot u _ { 2 }$ for each $\gamma$ .

Proof.
(1) We may assume the lift $\tilde { q }$ of $q$ is chosen so that $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) \in \langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 2 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ if and only if $N \geq 0$ .
Note that the rays spanned by $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ are irrational so $\mu _ { 1 } , \mu _ { 2 } \neq 0$ .
Suppose for a contradiction that there is an infinite sequence of broken lines $\gamma$ such that $m _ { \gamma } = \mu _ { 1 } w _ { 1 } + \mu _ { 2 } w _ { 2 }$ with $\mu _ { 2 } < 0$ .
Each broken line has at most $k$ bends and there are a finite number of $\Gamma$ -orbits of possible changes $\alpha \in M$ of the derivative of $\gamma$ at a bend; see Lemma 7.8 and its proof.
So, passing to a subsequence, we may assume that the bends (in order of increasing $t \in ( - \infty , 0 ] )$ of each $\gamma$ are of types $T ^ { \ast _ { 1 } } \alpha _ { 1 } , \dots , T ^ { \ast _ { l } } \alpha _ { l }$ f o r some fixed $\alpha _ { 1 } , \ldots , \alpha _ { l } \in M$ , $l \leq k$ , and $N \geq s _ { 1 } \geq s _ { 2 } \geq \cdot \cdot \cdot \geq s _ { l } \geq 0$ (depending on $\gamma$ ).
Say $N - s _ { i }$ is bounded for $i \leq l ^ { \prime }$ and unbounded otherwise.
Passing to a subsequence, we may assume that $N - s _ { i }$ is constant for $i \leq l ^ { \prime }$ .
Let $\gamma ^ { \prime }$ be the broken line obtained by truncating $\gamma$ after the first $l ^ { \prime }$ bends, and moving by a homothety so that (extending its final line segment) $\gamma ^ { \prime }$ ends at $\tilde { Q }$ .
Then $m _ { \gamma ^ { \prime } } = T ^ { N } ( m )$ for some fixed $m \in M$ .
Furthermore, $m _ { \gamma }$ is obtained from $m _ { \gamma ^ { \prime } }$ by adding a positive linear combination of $w _ { 1 }$ and $w _ { 2 }$ .
But since $\mu _ { 2 } < 0$ and $w _ { 1 } , w _ { 2 }$ are eigenvectors of $T$ with eigenvalues $\lambda ^ { - 1 } , \lambda$ , it follows that we must have $m = \nu _ { 1 } w _ { 1 } + \nu _ { 2 } w _ { 2 }$ with $\nu _ { 2 } < 0$ .
But then for sufficiently large $N$ , $T ^ { N } ( m )$ does not lie in the half-space $\mathbb { R } \cdot \tilde { Q } + \mathbb { R } _ { \ge 0 } \cdot w _ { 2 }$ .
This is a contradiction because $m _ { \gamma ^ { \prime } }$ always lies in this half-space.

To see that $| \mu _ { 1 } |$ is bounded, recall that $\begin{array} { r } { m _ { \gamma } = T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) - \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { l } T ^ { s _ { i } } \alpha _ { i } } \end{array}$ where $0 \leq l \leq k$ , $0 \leq s _ { i } \leq N$ , and the $\alpha _ { i }$ are selected from a finite set.
Now since $T w _ { 1 } = \lambda ^ { - 1 } w _ { 1 }$ it follows that $| \mu _ { 1 } |$ is bounded.

(2) Let $\mathfrak { u }$ be the connected component of $\tilde { B } _ { 0 } \backslash \mathrm { S u p p } _ { I } ( \tilde { \mathfrak { D } } )$ contained in $\tilde { \sigma }$ and containing $\ddot { \rho }$ in its closure.
Let $\tilde { Q } ^ { \prime } \in \mathfrak { u }$ be a point such that $\tilde { Q } ^ { \prime } \in \langle \tilde { \rho } , \tilde { Q } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ .
Then if $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) \in$ $\langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 2 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ and $\gamma ^ { \prime }$ is a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ , we obtain a broken line $\gamma$ for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ and $m _ { \gamma } = m _ { \gamma ^ { \prime } }$ as follows.
First apply a homothety to obtain a broken line passing through $\tilde { Q }$ , then truncate at $\tilde { Q }$ .
This gives an injective map between the set of broken lines for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } ) \in \langle \tilde { Q } , w _ { 2 } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ ending at ${ \tilde { Q } } ^ { \prime }$ with the set of such broken lines ending at $\tilde { Q }$ .

Now suppose $\gamma$ is a broken line for $T ^ { N } ( \tilde { q } )$ with endpoint $\tilde { Q }$ and $m _ { \gamma }$ not lying in the half-space $\lVert \boldsymbol { \cdot } \boldsymbol { u } _ { 1 } + \rVert _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } } \cdot u _ { 2 }$ .
Since $m _ { \gamma }$ lies in the half-space $\mathbb { R } \cdot \tilde { Q } + \mathbb { R } _ { \ge 0 } \cdot w _ { 2 }$ we find $m _ { \gamma }$ lies in the cone generated by $- \tilde { Q } , - u _ { 1 }$ .
In particular, $m _ { \gamma }$ does not lie in the half-space $\lVert \boldsymbol { \cdot } \boldsymbol { w } _ { 1 } + \rVert _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } } ^ { \mathrm { p } } w _ { 2 }$ , so by (1) there are only finitely many such $\gamma$ .
Now by the above construction it follows that for $\tilde { Q }$ sufficiently close to $\tilde { \rho }$ there are none.


7.4. Smoothness.
We will now complete the proof of:

Theorem 7.13. (Looijenga’s conjecture) Suppose that $\Bbbk = \mathbb { C }$ and the intersection matrix $( D _ { i } \cdot D _ { j } ) _ { 1 \leq i , j \leq n }$ is negative definite, so that $D \subset Y$ can be contracted to a cusp singularity $q \in Y ^ { \prime }$ .
Then the dual cusp to $q \in Y ^ { \prime }$ is smoothable.

We continue to work with the setup at the beginning of §7.2, with $L$ , $\sigma _ { P }$ , $P$ , $\mathfrak { m }$ and $J$ as given there.
By Theorem 7.7, if $I$ is a monomial ideal with $\sqrt { I } = J$ , we obtain a deformation $X _ { I }  S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ of $X _ { J }  S _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ .
For the remainder of the section, we shall write $S _ { I }$ for $S _ { I } ^ { \prime }$ .
Let $\mathfrak { f } _ { J } \colon \mathfrak { X } _ { J }  \mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ denote the formal deformation determined by the deformations $X _ { J ^ { N + 1 } }  \ S _ { J ^ { N + 1 } }$ for $N \geq 0$ .
Thus, $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ is the formal complex analytic space obtained as the completion of $S$ along $S _ { J }$ , $\mathfrak { X } _ { J }$ is a formal complex analytic space, and $\mathfrak { X } _ { J } \to \mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ is an adic flat morphism.
We similarly have the family $\mathfrak { X } _ { \mathfrak { m } } \to \mathfrak { S } _ { \mathfrak { m } }$ of formal schemes already studied in §4.
We refer to [G60] and [B78] for background on formal schemes and formal complex analytic spaces.

We have a section $s \colon S _ { J } \to X _ { J }$ such that, for $t \in S _ { J }$ general, the point $s ( t ) \in X _ { J , t }$ on the fibre is the cusp.
We write $X _ { J } ^ { o } : = X _ { J } \setminus s ( S _ { J } ) \subset X _ { J }$ and $X _ { I } ^ { o } \subset X _ { I }$ , $\mathfrak { X } _ { J } ^ { o } \subset \mathfrak { X } _ { J }$ for the induced open embeddings.

Let $Z _ { I } : = \operatorname { S i n g } ( f _ { I } ) \subset X _ { I }$ denote the singular locus of $f _ { I } \colon X _ { I } \to S _ { I }$ , see DefinitionLemma 4.1. Thus $Z _ { I } \subset X _ { I }$ is a closed embedding of schemes or complex analytic spaces.
Since the singular locus is compatible with base-change, the singular loci $Z _ { J ^ { n } } \subset X _ { J ^ { n } }$ determine a closed embedding $3 \mathrm { ~ J ~ } \subset \mathfrak { X } _ { J }$ which we refer to as the singular locus of $\mathfrak { f } _ { J } \colon \mathfrak { X } _ { J }  \mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ .

Lemma 7.14. In the above situation, there exists $0 \not = g \in \mathbb { k } \vert P \vert$ such that $\mathrm { S u p p } ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 . \ i } )$ is contained in $s ( S _ { J } )$ .
In particular, $\mathfrak { f } _ { J * } ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 _ { J } } )$ is a coherent sheaf on $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ .

Proof.
The proof is essentially the same as that of Lemma 4.5. Let $\mathfrak { U } _ { i , J }$ be defined as in (4.1).
Then $\mathfrak { X } _ { J } ^ { o }$ is a union of open subspaces $\mathfrak { V } _ { i , J }$ , $i = 1 , \ldots , n$ , such that $\mathfrak { V } _ { i , J }$ is an analytic open subspace of $\mathfrak { U } _ { i , J }$ for each $i$ .
We then take $g = u _ { 1 } \cdot \cdot \cdot u _ { n }$ as in the proof of Lemma 4.5, so that $\mathrm { S u p p } ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 J } )$ is contained in $s ( S _ { J } )$ .
So the support of $g \cdot ( \mathcal { O } _ { 3 J }$ is a closed subset of $s ( S _ { J } )$ , hence proper over $S _ { J }$ .
It follows that $\mathfrak { f } _ { J * } ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 J } )$ is coherent by [B78], 3.1. 

Let $u ( J )$ denote the natural map

$$
u ( J ) \colon { \mathcal { O } } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } } \to \mathfrak { f } _ { J * } ( { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 J } ) ,
$$

and $u ( { \mathfrak { m } } )$ similarly the natural map

$$
u ( \mathfrak { m } ) : \mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { \mathfrak { m } } } \to \mathfrak { f } _ { \mathfrak { m } * } ( \mathcal { O } _ { 3 _ { \mathfrak { m } } } ) .
$$

Lemma 7.15. $u ( J )$ is injective if and only if $u ( { \mathfrak { m } } )$ is injective.

Proof.
Let $0 \not = g \in \mathbb { k } | P |$ be the element given by Lemma 7.14. Let $\displaystyle { \mathcal { K } } _ { J }$ be the kernel of $u ( J )$ and $\mathcal { K } _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ the kernel of $g \cdot u ( J )$ .
Thus $\kappa _ { J } , \mathcal { K } _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ are ideal sheaves in $\langle \mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } }$ and $g \cdot K _ { J } ^ { \prime } \subset \mathcal { K } _ { J } \subset \mathcal { K } _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ .
The local rings of $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ are domains by Lemma 7.16, so ${ \cal { K } } _ { J } = 0$ if and only if ${ \cal { K } } _ { J } ^ { \prime } = 0$ .
The sheaf $\mathcal { K } _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ is coherent because the image of $g \cdot u ( J )$ is contained in the coherent subsheaf $\Sigma _ { J * } ( g \cdot { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 J } ) \subset \Sigma _ { J * } { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 J }$ .

We claim that the natural map

$$
{ \ K } _ { J } ^ { \prime } \otimes _ { { \mathcal { O } } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } } } { \mathcal { O } } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { \mathfrak { m } } } \to { \ K } _ { \mathfrak { m } } ^ { \prime }
$$

is an isomorphism.
Let $z \in \mathfrak { S } _ { \mathfrak { m } }$ be the unique point, coinciding with the zerodimensional torus orbit of $S$ , and let $\hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z }$ denote the completion of $\mathcal { O } _ { S , z }$ at its maximal ideal.
Note that $\hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z }$ coincides with $\mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { \mathfrak { m } } , z }$ and the completion of $\mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } , z }$ at its maximal ideal.
It suffices to show that the map

$$
K _ { J , z } ^ { \prime } \otimes _ { { \mathcal O } _ { { \mathfrak G } _ { J } , z } } { \hat { \mathcal O } } _ { S , z }  K _ { \mathfrak m , z } ^ { \prime }
$$

is an isomorphism.
We have an exact sequence of coherent sheaves

$$
0 \to { \mathcal { K } } _ { J } ^ { \prime } \to { \mathcal { O } } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } } \to { \mathfrak { f } } _ { J * } ( g \cdot { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 J } )
$$

and so an exact sequence of $\hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z }$ -modules

$$
0  { \mathcal { K } } _ { J , z } ^ { \prime } \otimes { \hat { \mathcal { O } } } _ { S , z }  { \hat { \mathcal { O } } } _ { S , z }  \mathfrak { f } _ { J * } ( g \cdot { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 J } ) _ { z } \otimes { \hat { \mathcal { O } } } _ { S , z } .
$$

Now

$$
\underline { { \dag } } _ { J * } ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 , J } ) _ { z } \otimes \hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z } = ( g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 , J } ) _ { s ( z ) } \otimes \hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z } = ( \widehat { g \cdot \mathcal { O } _ { 3 , J } } ) _ { s ( z ) } = g \cdot \hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 , { s ( z ) } }
$$

where the hats denote completion with respect to the maximal ideal of $\mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } , z }$ .
Thus $K _ { J , z } ^ { \prime } \otimes \hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z }$ is the kernel of the map

$$
\hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { S , z }  g \cdot \hat { \mathcal { O } } _ { 3 { \cal J } , s ( z ) } .
$$

By the base-change property for the singular locus, this map coincides with the corresponding map for $\mathfrak { m }$ .
This proves the claim.

The support of the ideal sheaf $\mathcal { K } _ { J } ^ { \prime }$ is either empty or $S _ { J }$ (because the local rings of $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ are domains and $S _ { J }$ is connected).
So ${ \cal { K } } _ { J } ^ { \prime } = 0$ if and only if ${ \cal { K } } _ { \mathfrak { m } } ^ { \prime } = 0$ by the claim.


Lemma 7.16. The local rings of $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ are integral domains.

Proof.
The completion of the local ring of $\mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ at a point $z \in S _ { J }$ is identified with the completion of the local ring of the toric variety $S$ at $z$ .
By Serre’s criterion for normality, the completion of a normal Noetherian ring at a maximal ideal is a local normal Noetherian ring; in particular, it is a domain.
Since $\mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } , z }$ is a local Noetherian ring, it is contained in its completion.
We deduce that $\mathcal { O } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } , z }$ is a domain.


Proof of Theorem 7.13. Let $f \colon Y \to Y ^ { \prime }$ be the contraction of $D \subset Y$ .
We may assume $f$ is the minimal resolution of $Y ^ { \prime }$ .
We may further assume $n \geq 3$ .
Indeed, the embedding dimension of the dual cusp equals $\operatorname* { m a x } ( n , 3 )$ by [N80], Corollary 7.8, p.
232 and [KM98], Theorem 4.57, p.
143, see also [L81], pg.
307. So in particular for $n \leq 3$ the dual cusp is a hypersurface and thus smoothable.
Let $L$ be a nef divisor on $Y$ such that N $[ \mathrm { E } ( Y ) _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } } \cap L ^ { \perp } = \langle D _ { 1 } , \dots , D _ { n } \rangle _ { \mathbb { R } _ { \geq 0 } }$ .
Let $\sigma _ { P } \subset A _ { 1 } ( Y , \mathbb { R } )$ be a strictly rational polyhedral cone containing $\mathrm { N E } ( Y )$ such that $\sigma _ { P } \cap L ^ { \perp }$ is a face of $\sigma _ { P }$ .
Let $P = \sigma _ { P } \cap A _ { 1 } ( Y , \mathbb { Z } )$ and $J = P \setminus P \cap L ^ { \perp }$ .
By Lemma 7.15 and Theorem 4.6, $u ( J )$ is not injective.

Let $x \in S _ { J }$ be a point lying in the interior of the toric variety $S _ { J }$ and $h \in { \mathcal { O } } _ { \mathfrak { S } _ { J } , x }$ a nonzero element of the kernel of $u ( J )$ near $x$ .
By Lemma 7.17 there is a morphism

$$
v \colon \mathrm { S p e c } \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } ) \to \mathfrak { S } _ { J }
$$

taking the unique point of the domain to $x$ and $0 \ \ne \ v ^ { * } ( h ) \ \in \ \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } )$ .
Let $Y / \operatorname { S p e c } ( \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } ) )$ be the pullback of $\mathfrak { X } _ { J } / \mathfrak { S } _ { J }$ by $\boldsymbol { v }$ and $Z \subset Y$ its singular locus.
Then $Y / \operatorname { S p e c } ( \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } ) )$ is a deformation of the dual cusp singularity.
Furthermore, $O _ { Z }$ is annihilated by $v ^ { * } ( h )$ , and the ideal generated by $v ^ { * } ( h )$ must contain $t ^ { N }$ , so $O _ { Z }$ is annihilated by $t ^ { N }$ .
By [A76], Theorem 5.1, there is an algebraic finite type deformation $Y ^ { \prime } / \operatorname { S p e c } \mathbb { C } \mathbb { \left[ t \right] }$ whose restriction to $\mathrm { S p e c } ( \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } ) )$ is locally analytically isomorphic to $Y / \operatorname { S p e c } ( \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } ) )$ .
Let $Z ^ { \prime } \subset Y ^ { \prime }$ denote the singular locus of $Y ^ { \prime } / \operatorname { S p e c } \mathbb { C } \mathbb { \left[ t \right] }$ .
Then $\mathcal { O } _ { Z ^ { \prime } }$ is a finite $\mathbb { C } \mathbb { \left[ t \right] } .$ -module because the fibre $Y _ { 0 } ^ { \prime }$ has an isolated singularity (using [Ma89], Theorem 8.4, p.
58).
Now $\mathcal { O } _ { Z } = \mathcal { O } _ { Z ^ { \prime } } / t ^ { N + 1 } \mathcal { O } _ { Z ^ { \prime } }$ and $t ^ { N } { \mathcal { O } } _ { Z } = 0$ , so $t ^ { N } \mathcal { O } _ { Z ^ { \prime } } = t ^ { N + 1 } \mathcal { O } _ { Z ^ { \prime } }$ and thus $t ^ { N } { \mathcal { O } } _ { Z ^ { \prime } } = 0$ by Nakayama’s lemma.
Hence the general fibre of $Y ^ { \prime } / \operatorname { S p e c } \mathbb { C } \mathbb { \left[ t \right] }$ is smooth, and $Y ^ { \prime } / \operatorname { S p e c } \mathbb { C } \mathbb { t } ]$ is a smoothing of the dual cusp.


Lemma 7.17. Let $A$ be the completion of a finitely generated normal Cohen-Macaulay $\mathbb { C }$ -algebra at a maximal ideal.
Let $0 \neq a \in A$ .
Then there exists $N \geq 0$ and a $\mathbb { C }$ -algebra map $f : A \to \mathbb { C } [ t ] / ( t ^ { N + 1 } )$ such that $f ( a ) \neq 0$ .

Proof.
Extend $a$ to a regular sequence $a , t _ { 1 } , \ldots , t _ { r }$ of length $\mathrm { d i m } A$ .
Then the normalization of $A / ( t _ { 1 } , \ldots , t _ { r } )$ is a finite direct sum of copies of $\mathbb { C } \left[ t \right]$ .
Now the result is clear.

